ARIE 1952-1953 [ARIE 071]

Annual Report on Indian Epigraphy for 1952-53. 1958. Delhi: Manager of Publications (Department of Archaeology).



APPENDIX A. LIST OF COPPER-PLATES, 1952-53.



BOMBAY
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/1 (page 22)
Place
Sri G.H.Khare, Curator, Bhārata Itihāsa Saṁśōdhaka Maṇḍala, Poona. Findspot —Tasgoan, Satara District.
Dynasty
Yādava
King
Kṛishṇa
Date
Śaka 1172 (nētra-adri-rudra), Sādhā-raṇa, Māgha, day of Purāri (i.e. ba. 14) = 1251 A.D., February 20.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Marāṭhī, Nāgarī.
Remarks
Registers a grant of the village Maṁjaravāṭaka by two brothers Chaṁdra and Kēśava, to the temple of Kalidēva built by them, under the stipulation that half the income of the village was to be utilised for eight kinds of bodily enjoyments of the god Kalidēva and the other half to be utilised for feeding 25 Brāhmaṇas. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXVII, p. 208 ff.
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/2 (page 22)
Place
The Director, B.J. Institute of Learning and Research, Gujarat Vidya Sabha, Ahmedabad. Findspot—Ladol, Mehsana District.
Dynasty
Chaulukya of Aṇa-hilapāṭaka.
King
Jayasiṁhadēva
Date
V.S. 1156, Ashāḍha śu 15, Monday = 1099 A.D., July 4, Monday, f.d.t. ·16.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Issued from Aṇahilapāṭaka. Records a grant of land measur-ing 4 vighas and 18 halavāhas in the vicinity of Gambhūta, by the king for maintaining a step-well constructed at Ṭākaudhī by Velahala, son of Mahāmātya Pajjaka, and the temple of Sumatināthadēva erected by Mahāmātya Yaśōrāja at Ṭākaudhī. Published in J. Or. Inst., Baroda, Vol. II, No. 4, p. 364.
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/3 (page 22)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Karṇadēva
Date
V.S. 1140, Pausha ba. 14, Monday = 1084 A.D., Janu-ary 8, Monday, f.d.t. ·43.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Issued from Dayāvaḍā. Registers a grant of land situated in the village Kāṇōḍā to Sumatināthadēva enshrined in the vasatikā erected by Mahāmātya Pradyumna in Ṭākavadhī, by the king who is styled Mahārājādhirāja and Trailōkyamalla. Loc. cit.


MADHYA PRADESH



ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/4 (page 22)
Place
Pandit L.P.Pandeya of the Mahākosal Historical Society, Raigarh. Findspot —Lodhiā, old Sarangarh State.
Dynasty
Sōmavaṁśa of Kosala
King
Mahāśivagupta, son of Harshadēva
Date
Year 57, Kārttika 30, Paurṇamī (in words and figures).
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Box-headed Characters.
Remarks
Registers the endowment of the village Vaidyapadraka in [O1]ṇī-bhōga to god Iśānēśvara-Bhaṭṭāraka of Khadirapadra-tala for worship, offerings, etc. The gift was made by the king at the request of Śrī-Śūlapāṇi-bhagavatpāda, a disciple of Śrī-Pramathāchārya, who hailed from Pañchayajña-tapōvana situated in Dvaitavana. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXVII, pp. 319 ff.


MADRAS
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/5 (page 22)
Place
Tahsildar of Dharmavaram. Findspot-Rāvulacheruvu, Anantapur District. Through Mr. N. Lakshminarayan Rao.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vijaya Bukkarāya
Date
Śaka 1109 (?) Jaya, Aśvija śu. 10.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
States that Bhōgi-nāyuḍu, Jikka-nāyuḍu, Jyōti-nāyuḍu and Anna-Chennama-nāyuḍu, sons of Mahānāyaṁkāchārya.. yākali Vīra-Bhōgi-nāyuḍu, having settled Nāgi-reḍḍi and Nārapa-reḍḍi, sons of Vōbi-reḍḍi, with half a share, and Kṛishṇa-reḍḍi and Veṅkaṭa-reḍḍi, sons of Nāgi-reḍḍi, with the other half share in Dharmavaram, the latter in turn settled several families of various professions such as the priest, the carpenter, the mason, etc., by gifts of land in the gift village. The tank and the temple of Chennakēśava at Dharmavaram are said to have been constructed by Chik-kavoḍeya of Ānegondi.
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/6 (page 23)
Place
Dr. R.Subrahmanyan, Asst. Superin-tendent, Department of Archaeology, Maharanipettah. Findspot—Urjām. Srikakulam District. From photographs.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga
King
Indravarman
Date
Year 97
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern Characters.
Remarks
Registers the gift of Hoñjēri-grāma in Krōshṭukavartanī, by the king to Mātṛichandraśarman, a Chhandōgabrahma-chārin of Vatsa-gōtra, on the day of Mahākārttika-Paurṇa-māsï. The record is stated to have been written by Āditya-mañchi, son of Vinayachandra, under the orders of Rājasiṁha. Mentions the ājñā (i.e. ājñapti) Ravichandra-mahattara.
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/7 (page 23)
Place
Do. Findspot—Niddham, Srikakulam District.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Dēvēndravarman Rājaraja
Date
Śaka 995 (śara-nidhi-nanda), Dhanus, Māgha śu. 13.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers the royal order regarding a grant of land in Māṭṭura-grāma in Saṁvā-vishaya to Nārāyaṇa, who seems to have been born of a vēśyā by name Vuddhamā. Some details of the dates of coronation of the king and his father Va-jrahasta are given (see introduction).
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/8 (page 23)
Place
Executive Officer, Aruṇāchalēśvarasvāmin Temple, Tiruvaṇṇāmalai, North Arcot District.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1613, Prajōt-patti, Tai 3.
Language & Alphabet
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the grant of the magamai on merchandise by Āyiravar Nagarattār headed by Pachchaiyappa Cheṭṭiyār of Maṇalūr-pēṭṭai for the mid-day service of god Aruṇāchalēśvara at Tiruvaṇṇāmalai and for charity at the maṭha.
ARIE/1952-1953/ A/1952-53/9 (page 23)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1710 (?), Kīlaka, Kārttigai 25, Satur-day, Uttiraṭṭādi = 1788 A.D., Decem-ber 6.
Language & Alphabet

GOKAK TALUK



ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/51 (page 31)
Place
Gokak Falls.—Mahāliṅgēśvara temple. Slab set up in the temple.
Dynasty
Kaḷachurya
King
…
Date
Śaka 1093, Vikṛiti, Māgha paurṇimā.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Damaged. Registers a gift for the repairs, etc., of the temple, when Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kaṭṭamadēva of the Raṭṭa family was governing Kūṁḍi Three Thousand. Seems to praise the exploits of the reigning king who is said to have van-quished the Chōḷa and Pāṇḍya kings and others. Details are lost.
ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/52 (page 32)
Place
Same slab
Dynasty
Kaḷachurya
King
Kalachurya-chakravarti Bhujabala-malla.
Date
Year... Paushya śu. 11, Monday, Uttarāyaṇa-saṅ-kramaṇa.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Damaged. Records the grant of the village Koṁḍanūr situated in the Kuṁdurige kaṁpaṇa of Kūṁḍi Three Thousand for offerings, etc., to god Taṭēśvara of the Mahā-tīrtha by the king's officer Pergaḍe Dhannugidēva in conjunc-tion with the Karaṇas, with the consent of the king. Amṛita-rāśi was the recipient of the gift.

ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/54 (page 32)
Place
Koṇṇūr.—Jaina temple. Slab kept in the temple.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa.
King
Tribhuvanamalla (Vikramāditya VI)
Date
Chālukya-Vikrama year 12, Prabhava, Pausha ba. 14, Vaḍḍavāra, Utta-rāyaṇa-saṁ-krānti = 1087 A.D., December 25, Saturday, f.d.t. ·86.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers a gift of land, houses, etc., made by Mahāprabhu Nidhiyama-gāvuṇḍa for the benefit of the Jaina temple constructed by him at Koṁḍanūr. The donor belonged to Balātkāra-gaṇa of Mūla-saṁgha and the genea-logical account of his preceptors is narrated at length. The Chālukya prince Jayakarṇa and the Raṭṭa chief Sēna are also eulogised. Published in JBBRAS, Vol. X, pp. 287 ff.
ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/55 (page 32)
Place
Same slab
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Chālukya-Vikrama year 46, Plava, Pushya śu. 13.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Damaged. Registers a gift made to the sage Vāsupūjya for the benefit of the Jaina temple constructed by Jayakarṇa, the beloved son of Vikramachakri. Ibid, pp. 287 ff.

ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/63 (page 33)
Place
Slab lying on the tank bund outside the village.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa.
King
Tribuvanamalla (Vikramāditya VI)
Date
Chālukya-Vikrama year 5, Raudri, Chaitra, Sunday.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Damaged. Registers a gift of land made into the hands of the two hundred Mahājanas of the agrahāra of Savaṇūr headed by Daṇḍanāyaka Kēsimayya, possibly by the Paṭṭa ṇādhipati of rājadhāni Baṅkāpura, when Mahāpradhāna Hērisandhivigrahi Daṇḍanāyaka (name lost), a faithful warrior (Pēshaṇa-Hanumān) of Vīra-Noḷaṁba-Pallava Permā-naḍi, was governing the agrahāra of Savaṇūr, Sāntaḷige-Thousand and Nāgarakhaṇḍa-Seventy which comprised a kampaṇa of Banavāsi-nāḍu. Pergaḍe Siṁgimayya wrote the record with chalk on the stone and Rēvavōja incised it.

RON TALUK



ARIE/1952-1953/B/1952-53/102 (page 36)
Place
Iṭagi.—Śambhuliṅga temple. Stone in the temple.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Kalyāṇa
King
Trailōkyamalla
Date
Śaka 976, Jaya, Jyēshṭha amāvāsyā, solar eclipse = 1054 A.D., May 10, Tues-day, solar eclipse.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
States that the mahāgrahāra Iṭṭage included in the Kisukāḍu-nāḍu was the native place of the king's subordinate Śrīpati-chamūpa. Describes the Mahājanas of the village and the teacher Bonteyadēva who belonged to this place and resided at Kanakapura (i.e., Hoṁbaḷ). Registers a gift of land to the teacher Mallikārjuna, disciple of Bonteyadēva, for god Svayaṁbhū by the Mahājanas of the place headed by the Üroḍeya. Also registers gifts to the same god made by Üroḍeya Vikkarasa of Kisukāḍu-nāḍu, the residents of Honneganūr and others.

A verse in the Śārdūlavikrīḍita metre in which a certain Sarva-dēva claims to have calculated the longevity of the beings thus: nāga and male lāvaka 120 years; aśva 32 years; khara, gō and mahisha 25 years; mēsha, chhāga and mṛiga, 16 years; and śvā 12 years. In characters of about the eleventh century.

Dynasty
…
King
Jayasiṁha
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Kannaḍa (verse), Grantha & Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the gift of a piece of land made by the king to Mōchabbarasī as kanyādāna, i.e. a gift to a damsel. Ind., Vol. XXIX, p. 203 ff. and Plate. In characters of about the 10th century.

Tamil
Remarks
Seems to register the purchase and gift of land by Tiruvananta-mutti Aruḷāḷaṉ alias Vīraräjēndra-Pallavaṟaiyaṉ, constituting the gift lands into a brahmadēya called Aiyiṇḍambākkiḻāṉ-brahmadēyam after his own name in the 24th year of the reign of a king (name lost). Refers to certain transactions made during some specitied regnal years of Suṅgantavirttaruḷiṉa Kulōttuṅgachōḷa. Among the assignees of land so given is mentioned the piḍāri (goddess) Aiyapoḻil-Mākāḷi of Nagai-kkumāṅguḍi alias Rājēndrachōḷapuram and among the signatories figure Kāliṅgarāyar and Vāṇādhirājar.

Telugu
Remarks
Records that the pair of gold anklets with tinkling bells (gej-jelu) is the offering of Peda-Veṅkaṭaperumāḷ-Nāyanivāru, son of Lakshmidēvammavāru, the queen (paṭṭamahishī) of Tupākula Rāmaliṅgayya-Nāyanivāru. The weight of the set is given as 468(1/4) varāha. …
King
…

Language & Alphabet

Refers to the reign of Tatāra Khāna and mentions his subor-dinate (name not clear) who ruled over Jata-haḍā-nagara. Also mentions Kalāvanta and refers to a step-well (vāpī). For the Persian portion, see Appendix C, No. 160.
